Famous Opening Lines in the Plays of Shakespeare
7. Which play opens with "Let fame, that all hunt
after in their lives."?
A) Richard III
B) Love's Labour's Lost
C) Twelfth Night
D) Cymbeline
Answer: B)

summer by this son of York." is the opening line of
which play?
A) Richard III
B) Titus Andronicus
C) Timon of Athens
D) Pericles
Answer: A)

A) Twelfth Night
B) Troilus and Cressida
C) Timon of Athens
D) Two Gentlemen of Verona
Answer: C)

C) Cymbeline
D) Twelfth Night
Answer: D)

1. Who wrote the sonnet "Shakespeare" in 1849?
a) John Aubrey
b) William Wordsworth
c) Matthew Arnold
d) Samuel Johnson
Answer: c) Matthew Arnold

shaped man"?
a) Ben Jonson
b) John Aubrey
c) Thomas Gray
d) Coleridge
Answer: b) John Aubrey
3. Who wrote "With the same key Shakespeare
unlocked his heart, once more!" in "Scorn Not the
Sonnet"?
a) Milton
b) Alexander Pope
c) William Wordsworth
d) Robert Greene
Answer: c) William Wordsworth
4. Who referred to Shakespeare as "Our myriad-
minded Shakespeare"?
a) Ben Jonson
b) John Dryden
c) Coleridge
d) Samuel Johnson
Answer: c) Coleridge

comic wit degenerating into clenches, his serious

a) Samuel Johnson
b) Thomas Gray
c) John Dryden
d) Ben Jonson
Answer: c) John Dryden

d) Matthew Arnold
Answer: a) Samuel Johnson

d) John Aubrey

1. What is the full title of Milton's first anti-prelatical
tract?
a) Of Reformation in England and the Causes That
Hitherto Hindered It
b) The Judgement of Dr Reynolds Touching the
Originals of Episcopacy
c) The Role of Church Government
d) The Simplicity and Clarity of Scriptures
Answer: a) Of Reformation in England and the
Causes That Hitherto Hindered It
2. What did Milton want to reform in his first anti-
prelatical tract?
a) The monarchy
b) The Church of England
c) Both the monarchy and the Church of England
d) The Presbyterian system
Answer: c) Both the monarchy and the Church of
England
3. Which king's reign did Milton examine for
historical changes in the Church of England?
a) Charles I
b) James I
c) Henry VIII
d) Elizabeth I
Answer: c) Henry VIII
4. What did Milton criticize about the Church of
England in his first tract?
a) Its simplicity and clarity
b) Its resemblance to the Roman Catholic Church
c) Its support for republicanism
d) Its lack of hierarchy
Answer: b) Its resemblance to the Roman Catholic
Church
5. What type of government did Milton assert
influenced the structure of the Church of England?
a) Monarchical civil government
b) Democratic government
c) Republican government
d) Federal government
Answer: a) Monarchical civil government
6. What concept did Milton use as a metaphor for his
analysis of religion in "Of Reformation"?
a) The mind
b) The body
c) The soul
d) The heart
Answer: b) The body
7. What system of church governance did Milton
favor in "Of Reformation"?
a) Episcopal system
b) Hierarchical system
c) Presbyterian system
d) Democratic system
Answer: c) Presbyterian system
8. What did Milton believe should be the relationship
between the soul and spiritual truth?
a) Intermediated by the government
b) Direct relationship without intermediaries
c) Governed by bishops
d) Controlled by the organized church
Answer: b) Direct relationship without
intermediaries
9. How did Milton view the physical construction of
religious truth?
a) Through the hierarchy of the church
b) Through scripture
c) Through government intervention
d) Through bishops and presbyters
Answer: b) Through scripture
10. What was the primary purpose of 'reformation'
according to Milton?
a) To establish a hierarchical system
b) To restore the ideas of the proper place
c) To increase government control
d) To support the monarchy
Answer: b) To restore the ideas of the proper place
11. What is the title of Milton's second anti-prelatical
tract?
a) Of Reformation
b) Of Prelatical Episcopacy
c) The Judgement of Dr Reynolds Touching the
Originals of Episcopacy
d) The Role of Church Government
Answer: b) Of Prelatical Episcopacy
12. What prompted Milton to write "Of Prelatical
Episcopacy"?
a) A sermon by William Laud
b) The Root and Branch Petition
c) The Judgement of Dr Reynolds Touching the
Originals of Episcopacy by James Usher
d) A decree by Charles 1
Answer: c) The Judgement of Dr Reynolds Touching
the Originals of Episcopacy by James Usher
13. According to Milton, how can religious truth be
attained?
a) Through bishops
b) Through government intermediaries
c) Through scripture alone
d) Through the organized church
Answer: c) Through scripture alone
14. What did Milton assert about the difference
between a bishop and a presbyter?
a) There is a significant difference
b) They are completely different
c) There is no difference
d) One is superior to the other
Answer: c) There is no difference
15. What did Milton oppose in the establishment of
the church?
a) Governance by individual congregations
b) Hierarchical system by bishops
c) Republicanism
d) Simplicity and clarity of scriptures
Answer: b) Hierarchical system by bishops
1. What is the title of Milton's third anti-prelatical
tract?
a) Of Reformation
b) Of Prelatical Episcopacy
c) Animadversions: Upon the Remonstrants
Defence, Against Semectymnuus
d) The Reason of Church Government Urged Under

b) Attacking Joseph Hall's personal views
c) Supporting Episcopacy
d) Promoting the monarchy
Answer: b) Attacking Joseph Hall's personal views
3. What did Milton argue was more important than
any other consideration in religion?

b) Individual reading of the Bible
c) Government intervention
d) Rituals and set forms

advocate for in his third tract?

b) Monarchical church governance

d) Democratic system
Answer: c) Direct relationship between preacher
and congregation
5. What is the title of Milton's fourth anti-prelatical

b) Of Prelatical Episcopacy

d) The Reason of Church Government Urged Under

Milton's fourth tract?
a) The nature of political hierarchies
b) The role of bishops
c) Language and the form of truth
d) The importance of rituals
Answer: c) Language and the form of truth
7. Which system did Milton endorse as a replacement
for the episcopal hierarchy in his fourth tract?
a) Episcopal system.
b) Presbyterian system
c) Democratic system.
d) Monarchical system.
Answer: b) Presbyterian system
8. What is the title of Milton's fifth anti-prelatical
tract?

b) Of Prelatical Episcopacy
c) An Apology for Semectymnuus
d) The Reason of Church Government Urged Under

Answer: c) An Apology for Semectymnuus
9. What did Milton argue was a consequence of
defending the truth in his fifth tract?
a) Increased popularity
b) Personal attacks
c) Political support
d) Financial reward
Answer: b) Personal attacks
10. What did Milton praise as a way to hinder a
dictatorial monarchy in his fifth tract?
a) The episcopal hierarchy
b) The formation of parliament
c) The role of bishops
d) The preservation of rituals
Answer: b) The formation of parliament
1. What prompted Milton to publish his divorce
tracts?
a) His marriage to Catherine Woodcock
b) His wife's infidelity
c) His wife Mary Powell deserting him
d) Financial troubles
Answer: c) His wife Mary Powell deserting him
10. How many divorce tracts did Milton publish?
a) Two
b) Three
c) Four
d) Five
Answer: c) Four
3. What was the broader context for the publication
of Milton's divorce tracts?
a) Reforming financial laws
b) Reforming divorce laws
c) Reforming political policies
d) Reforming religious practices
Answer: b) Reforming divorce laws
4, Which tract was addressed to the Parliament and
the Westminster Assembly of Divines?
a) The Judgement of Martin Bucer
b) Tetrachordon
c) Colasterian
d) The Doctrine and Discipline of Divorce
Answer: d) The Doctrine and Discipline of Divorce
5. In "The Doctrine and Discipline of Divorce," what
did Milton argue a true marriage consists of?
a) Financial compatibility
b) Mind and body compatibility
c) Social status
d) Political views
Answer: b) Mind and body compatibility
6. What did Milton believe about those inaptly joined
in marriage?
a) They should stay together
b) They should have separate lives
c) They should be allowed to divorce
d) They should be punished
Answer: c) They should be allowed to divorce

Answer: d) Sublimity as an aesthetic concept

How did John Keats feel about Milton's style?
a) He found it suitable for all poets
b) He found it unsuitable and overly complex
c) He admired it without reservations
d) He found it simple and direct
Answer: b) He found it unsuitable and overly
complex
9. What did Sandra Gilbert and Susan Gubar opine
about Mary Shelley's novel "Frankenstein" in "The
Madwoman in the Attic"?
a) It was a key 'Romantic' reading of "Paradise Lost"
b) It was not influenced by "Paradise Lost"
c) It was solely a gothic novel
d) It was inspired by "The Faerie Queene"
Answer: a) It was a key ‘Romantic’ reading of
"Paradise Lost"
10. Who published an extensive edition of Milton's
poetical works in 1749?
a) Samuel Johnson
b) T.S. Eliot
c) Thomas Newton
d) Percy Bysshe Shelley
Answer: c) Thomas Newton
11. What did Voltaire say about Milton in "The Age of
Louis XIV"?
a) He was a minor poet
b) He was overrated
c) He was the glory and the wonder of England
d) He was insignificant
Answer: c) He was the glory and the wonder of
England
12. How did Samuel Johnson describe "Paradise Lost"?
a) A poem with little importance
b) A poem that may claim the first place in design
c) A poem that was difficult to read
d) A poem that was not influential
Answer: b) A poem that may claim the first place in
design
13. What did Percy Bysshe Shelley write about
Milton's God and Devil?
a) Milton's God was superior to his Devil
b) Milton's Devil had no moral virtue
c) Milton alleged no superiority of moral virtue to
his God over his Devil
d) Milton's God was inferior to his Devil
Answer: c) Milton alleged no superiority of moral
virtue to his God over his Devil
14. According to C. S. Lewis in his "Preface to Paradise
Lost," what can every poem be considered as?
a) A simple story
b) An organization of words to produce a patterned
experience
c) A political statement
d) A historical document
Answer: b) An organization of words to produce a
patterned experience
15. What does Lewalski write about Satan's rhetoric
of republicanism in "Paradise Lost"?
a) It signals Milton's approval of his party
b) It signals Milton's profound disillusion with his
own party and political discourse generally
c) It signals Milton's indifference to political
matters
d) It signals Milton's support for monarchy
Answer: b) It signals Milton's profound disillusion
with his own party and political discourse generally
16. What did Isaac Watts say about Milton in 1734?
a) He was not influential in poetry
b) He was the parent and author of blank verse
among us
c) He wrote only in rhyme
d) He was better known for his prose
Answer: b) He was the parent and author of blank
verse among us
17. What did Dr. Johnson say about Milton's similes?
a) They were less numerous and more varied than
those of his predecessors
b) They were monotonous and repetitive
c) They were more common than those of his
predecessors
d) They were simple and direct
Answer: a) They were less numerous and more
varied than those of his predecessors

- A) The horrors of war and the peace time recovery
- B) The journey of self-discovery
- C) The clash between old and new wealth
- D) The intricacies of love and marriage
- Answer: A) The horrors of war and the peace time
recovery
25. Whois the victim of the robbery in "Loyalties"?
- A) A middle-aged novelist
- B) A wealthy businessman
-C) Arich Jew
-D) A politician
- Answer: C) Arich Jew
26. What does "Loyalties" primarily attack?
- A) Gender discrimination
- B) Racial inequality
- C) Class prejudices and anti-Semitism
- D) Political corruption
- Answer: C) Class prejudices and anti-Semitism
27. What societal issue is highlighted in "Fraternity"?
- A) The hypocrisy of social conventions
- B) The heroism of individuals in war
- C) The journey of self-discovery
- D) The rise of the industrial age
- Answer: A) The hypocrisy of social conventions
28. What prevents the middle-aged novelist in

from the slums?

- B) Lack of love
- C) Financial difficulties
- D) Personal health issues
- Answer: A) Fear of societal disapproval

- C) The Patrician
- D) Justice
- Answer: A) A Bit O' Love
49. Where can you find the quotation: "Beauty means
this to one person, perhaps, and that to another. And
yet when any one of us has seen or heard or read that
which to him is beautiful, he has known an emotion
which is in every case the same in kind, if not in
degree"?
- A) Candelabra
- B) Vague Thoughts on Art
- C) The Dark Flower
- D) Studies and Essays
- Answer: A) Candelabra
50. Which work contains the following quote: "Only
out of stir and change is born new salvation. To deny
that is to deny belief in man, to turn our backs on
courage"?
- A) The Forsyte Saga
- B) Saint's Progress
- C) Studies and Essays
- D) Vague Thoughts on Art
- Answer: D) Vague Thoughts on Art
51. Which work contains the quotation: "Dawn has
power to fertilise the most matter-of-fact vision"?
- A) Over the River
- B) The Forsyte Saga
- C) The White Monkey
- D) Fraternity
- Answer: B) The Forsyte Saga
52. In which work does the following quote appear:
"He is but a poor philosopher who holds a view so
narrow as to exclude forms not to his personal taste"?
- A) Studies and Essays
- B) Vague Thoughts on Art
- C) The Forsyte Saga
- D) Candelabra
- Answer: B) Vague Thoughts on Art
53. Where can you find the quote: "Society is built on
marriage... marriage and its consequences"?
- A) The White Monkey
- B) The Forsyte Saga
- C) Justice
- D) Fraternity
- Answer: B) The Forsyte Saga
54. Which work contains the following quote:
"Where Beauty was, nothing ever ran quite straight,
which, no doubt, was why so many people looked on
it as immoral"?
- A) The Forsyte Saga
- B) The White Monkey
- C) Over the River
- D) Flowering Wilderness
- Answer: A) The Forsyte Saga
55. In which work does this quote appear: "It was
such a spring day as breathes into a man an ineffable
yearning, a painful sweetness, a longing that makes
him stand motionless, looking at the leaves or grass,
and fling out his arms to embrace he knows not
what"?
- A) The Forsyte Saga
- B) The White Monkey
- C) Studies and Essays
- D) Fraternity
- Answer: A) The Forsyte Saga
56. Where can you find the quotation: "Love could
never come to full fruition till it was destroyed"?
- A) The Dark Flower
- B) Fraternity
- C) Beyond
- D) The Forsyte Saga
- Answer: B) Fraternity
57. Which work contains the following quote: "It
is not good enough to spend a time and ink in
describing the penultimate sensations and physical
movements of people getting into a state of rut, we all
know them so well"?
- A) Over the River
- B) Justice
- C) Studies and Essays
- D) Letter to Edward Garnett about DH Lawrence's
Sons and Lovers
- Answer: D) Letter to Edward Garnett about DH
Lawrence's Sons and Lovers
58. In which work does the quote: "It isn't enough to
love people because they're good to you, or because in
some way or other you're going to get something by
it. We have to love because we love loving" appear?
- A) Bit of Love
- B) The Forsyte Saga
- C) The White Monkey
- D) Over the River
- Answer: A) Bit of Love
59. Where can you find the quotation: "The
beginnings and endings of all human undertakings
are untidy, the building of a house, the writing of
novel, the demolition of the bridge, and, eminently,
the finish of a voyage"?
- A) The Forsyte Saga
- B) Over the River
- C) Studies and Essays
- D) Vague Thoughts on Art
- Answer: B) Over the River
60. Which work contains the following quote:
"Religion was nearly dead because there was no
longer real belief in future life; but something was
struggling to take its place service - social service the
ant's creed, the bees' creed"?
- A) Over the River
- B) The Forsyte Saga
- C) Fraternity
- D) The White Monkey
- Answer: A) Over the River
61. In which work does the quote: "Everything known
before it happens; the headlines twice the size of the
events" appear?
- A) The Forsyte Saga
- B) Over the River
-C) Justice
- D) Bit of Love
- Answer: B) Over the River
62. Where can you find the quotation: "How to save
the old that's worth saving, whether in landscape,
houses, manners, institutions, or human type, is one
of the greatest problems, and the one that we bother
least about"?
- A) The Forsyte Saga
- B) Studies and Essays
- C) Vague Thoughts on Art
- D) Over the River
- Answer: D) Over the River
63. Which work contains the following quote:
"Naturalistic art is like steady lamp, held up from
time to time, in whole light things will be seen to a
space; clearly and in due proportion, freed from the
mists of prejudice or partisanship"?
- A) Studies and Essays
- B) Vague Thoughts on Art
- C) Candelabra
- D) On Some Platitudes Concerning Drama
- Answer: D) On Some Platitudes Concerning
Drama
